[05/02/26, 05:08] Vardhan Iith ES'26: Let the sage who was mentioned be A, and the other two B and C.
If anyone saw two white hats, they would have immediately concluded theirs to be blue, and would have shouted it out. This did not happen, so there are at least two blue hats. A saw this, so A knows this. C did not shout тАШblueтАЩ immediately, so B knows that either A or B or both have blue. Similarly for C.
If A was white: since C did not shout blue immediately, B knows that his must be blue (since two whites seen implies immediate тАШblueтАЩ callout). Similarly for C. So B and C would have called out blue (whoever processed this stage first, after theyтАЩre assured that the other processed stage 1). This did not happen.
If A was blue: everyone sees two blue hats. It has been long enough for everyone to process the first two stages, and no one said anything, so they all know that they have blue hats on. Whoever shouts тАШblueтАЩ first, will be the kingтАЩs advisor.
According to the narration, A is the first to do so.
